Make a Plotter-based 2D scatter for a `Collection` of `Point`s\n\nAnalogous to `sequoiaSearchResults`, we first write a method that **returns a chart**:\n\n```smalltalk\nCollection>>asGtPlotter2DScatter\n    <gtExample>\n    <return: #GtPlotterScatterChart>  \"adjust if your class name differs\"\n    | theData xMax yMax xScale yScale chart |\n\n    \"Assume self is a collection of Points\"\n    self isEmpty ifTrue: [ ^ GtPlotterScatterChart new ].\n\n    theData := GtPlotterDataGroup new values: self.\n    theData := theData labelled: [ :p | p printString ].\n\n    xMax := self inject: 0 into: [ :max :p | max max: p x ].\n    yMax := self inject: 0 into: [ :max :p | max max: p y ].\n\n    xScale := GtPlotterLinearScale new\n        domainFrom: 0\n        to: xMax.\n\n    yScale := GtPlotterLinearScale new\n        domainFrom: 0\n        to: yMax.\n\n    chart := GtPlotterScatterChart new.\n    chart\n        xScale: xScale;\n        yScale: yScale;\n        xData: [ :p | p x ];\n        yData: [ :p | p y ];\n        with: theData.\n\n    ^ chart\n```\n\nNotes:\n\n* This mirrors `sequoiaSearchResults`:\n\n  * build `GtPlotterDataGroup`\n  * compute max values → `GtPlotterLinearScale`\n  * configure chart with data blocks\n  * `with:` the data group\n* If your image doesn’t have `GtPlotterScatterChart`, look in the browser for classes next to `GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart` (e.g. `GtPlotterPointChart` / `GtPlotterCartesianChart`) and swap the class + `xData:/yData:` selectors accordingly. The pattern stays identical.\n\nYou can already test this directly:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10. 50@20. 30@80 } asGtPlotter2DScatter\n```\n\nand inspect the result.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Wire it into a GT view (`gtScatter2DOn:`)\n\nNow hook this chart into the inspector, the same way the JSON view does it:\n\n```smalltalk\nCollection>>gtScatter2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView forward\n        title: '2D Input Space';\n        object: [ self asGtPlotter2DScatter ];\n        view: #gtInspectorViewFor:context:\n```\n\n(If your GT doesn’t know `#gtInspectorViewFor:context:`, pick any of the view symbols used in `GtPlotterHorizontalBarChartExamples` — e.g. open `sequoiaSearchResults`, press ⌘+N on the example result and see which view method it uses; plug that selector in instead.)\n\nNow:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10 . 50@20 . 30@80 } inspect\n```\n\nand choose **2D Input Space** → you should get a Plotter scatter: three dots at the appropriate coordinates, scaled to the chart.\n\n---\n\nOnce this works, you can copy the exact same pattern for:\n\n```smalltalk\nKohonenSom>>gtWeights2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView forward\n        title: 'Weights (2D)';\n        object: [ self weightsAsPoints2D asGtPlotter2DScatter ];\n        view: #gtInspectorViewFor:context:\n```\n\n(where `asGtPlotter2DScatter` lives on `Collection` as above).\n\nThat keeps everything in the **Plotter world**, exactly like `sequoiaSearchResults`, and avoids the Mondrian/Bloc version-mismatch headaches.\n"

				"string" : "You’re absolutely right to call me out on the guessing – thanks for that.\nLet’s stop inventing APIs and **only use what we *know* exists** in your image:\n\n* The exact Plotter API from\n  `GtPlotterHorizontalBarChartExamples>>sequoiaSearchResults`\n\nNo `xData:`, no scatter classes, no fancy layouts, no `isKindOf:` tricks.\n\nWe’ll build a tiny **horizontal bar chart** for a collection of `Point`s, using only:\n\n* `GtPlotterDataGroup`\n* `labelled:`\n* `background:`\n* `inject:intoValues:`\n* `GtPlotterLinearScale new domainFrom:to:`\n* `GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart`\n* `barLabelSpacing:`\n* `barWidthScale:`\n* `barWidthData:`\n* `amountOfTicks:`\n* `with:`\n\n…and nothing else.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Put the helper on `Array` (no abstract Collection involved)\n\nDefine this **exactly** on `Array` (class: `Array`, protocol whatever you like):\n\n```smalltalk\nArray>>asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart\n    <gtExample>\n    <return: #GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart>\n    | records theData maxX xScale chart |\n\n    \"Assume self is an Array of Points (x@y).\"\n    self isEmpty ifTrue: [ ^ GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart new ].\n\n    \"Step 1: turn points into small dictionaries with #index and #x/#y.\"\n    records := OrderedCollection new.\n    1 to: self size do: [ :idx |\n        | p |\n        p := self at: idx.\n        records add: (Dictionary newFrom: {\n            #index -> idx.\n            #x     -> p x.\n            #y     -> p y }) ].\n\n    \"Step 2: GtPlotterDataGroup like sequoiaSearchResults.\"\n    theData := GtPlotterDataGroup new values: records.\n\n    theData := theData\n        labelled: [ :each | 'p', (each at: #index) asString ].\n\n    theData := theData\n        background: [ :each |\n            \"For now, just use a single colour (we *could* use #y if wanted).\"\n            Color\n                r: 66\n                g: 188\n                b: 238\n                range: 255 ].\n\n    \"Step 3: same scale pattern as sequoiaSearchResults.\"\n    maxX := theData\n        inject: 0\n        intoValues: [ :currentMax :each |\n            currentMax max: (each at: #x) ].\n\n    xScale := GtPlotterLinearScale new\n        domainFrom: 0\n        to: maxX.\n\n    \"Step 4: build the bar chart using only known selectors.\"\n    chart := GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart new.\n    chart\n        barLabelSpacing: 50;\n        barWidthScale: xScale;\n        barWidthData: [ :each | each at: #x ];\n        amountOfTicks: 4;\n        with: theData.\n\n    ^ chart\n```\n\nThis is deliberately boring and conservative:\n\n* no `collectWithIndex:`\n* no type checks\n* no other classes than those you *already showed* in `sequoiaSearchResults`.\n\n### Test it **before** wiring any `gtView`\n\nIn a playground:\n\n```smalltalk\n#( 10@10 50@20 30@80 ) asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart\n```\n\nEvaluate and inspect the result. You should see a **horizontal bar chart** with three bars:\n\n* bar lengths: 10, 50, 30 (x-coordinates)\n* labels: `p1`, `p2`, `p3`\n\nIf you see *any* error here, the top frame will tell us exactly which message is missing, and it’ll be from **this method only**, which we can then fix deterministically (no guessing).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Hook it into the inspector (optional, but likely what you want)\n\nOnce the helper works, you can wire your `Collection>>gtScatter2DOn:` like this:\n\n```smalltalk\nArray>>gtScatter2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView forward\n        title: '2D Input Space';\n        object: [ self asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart ];\n        view: #gtInspectorViewFor:context:\n```\n\nAgain: **put this on `Array`**, not `Collection`. That completely avoids the `Collection had the subclass responsibility to implement #do:` trap.\n\nThen:\n\n```smalltalk\n#( 10@10 50@20 30@80 ) inspect\n```\n\nChoose **2D Input Space** → you get the same bar chart, now as a GT view.\n\n---\n\n## 3. How this relates back to SOM\n\nFor SOM:\n\n* `weightsAsPoints2D` should produce an `Array` of `Point`s.\n* You can reuse the same helper:\n\n```smalltalk\nKohonenSom>>gtWeights2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView forward\n        title: 'Weights (Input Space, 1D-projected)';\n        object: [ self weightsAsPoints2D asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart ];\n        view: #gtInspectorViewFor:context:\n```\n\nThis gives you at least a **stable Plotter-based visualization** of weights vs. neuron index along one dimension, using only APIs we’re certain exist.\n\nIf you’re up for it, the next step *after this is confirmed working* is to look in your image for a Plotter class that does genuine 2D coordinates (scatter/point/cartesian) and adjust the chart-building method accordingly — but that will be done by *inspecting the classes in your image*, not by me free-styling new selectors.\n\nFor now, the goal is: **no more abstract Collection errors, no more missing messages, only code built from the sequoia example.**\n"
			}
		]

SOM is “just” a set of prototype vectors (*codebook vectors*).\n* Each prototype lives in input space.\n\n### 0.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.1–3.2**:\n\n* “Reference vectors”\n* The SOM as *moving representative prototypes*\n\n---\n\n# 🟧 STAGE 1 — Points in Input Space (Unscaled)\n\n**This is where your original `weightsAsPoints2D` view sits.**\n\n### 1.1 Concept\n\nProject each N-dimensional weight vector to 2D input space — only works because you start with **inputDimension = 2**.\n\n### 1.2 GT View\n\n`weightsAsPoints2D`\n\n* Draw dots at (x,y).\n* No scaling.\n* No zoom.\n* No grid.\n\n### 1.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* Codebook vectors occupy *regions* in input space.\n* Their shape is arbitrary at init.\n\n### 1.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.4.1 – Ordering of Reference Vectors in the Input Space**\nThis is exactly what this view corresponds to.\n\n---\n\n# 🟩 STAGE 2 — Scaled Input Space Projection\n\n**Your current “2D Input Space” tab belongs here.**\n\n### 2.1 Concept\n\nSame as Stage 1, but:\n\n* Add zoom\n* Keep origin fixed\n* Fit into a fixed pixel canvas\n\n### 2.2 GT View (rename!)\n\nRename from:\n❌ *2D Input Space*\nTo the correct name:\n\n### **“Mapped Points in Input Space”**\n\n### 2.3 Why this name?\n\nBecause this view does **not** show the SOM grid;\nit only shows **the mapped codebook vectors**, i.e. the *topology in input space*.\nThis is representation #2 in Kohonen’s terminology.\n\n### 2.4 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* Why untrained SOM codebook vectors form strange shapes (e.g. “butterfly”)\n* Why training gradually straightens the manifold\n* Why distances in input space matter for early organization\n\n### 2.5 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.4.1** and Fig. 3.5 (ordering demonstration in input space).\nThis is a direct counterpart.\n\n---\n\n# 🟦 STAGE 3 — SOM Grid Coordinates (Output Space)\n\n### 3.1 Concept\n\nEach node i has:\n\n* A location on the *map grid* (usually a 2D lattice)\n* A vector in input space (the codebook vector)\n\nThis view shows only the **grid layout**.\n\n### 3.2 GT View\n\n`gridCoordinates2D`\n\n* Draw each unit at its (i,j) lattice coordinate\n* No weights yet\n\n### 3.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* The SOM output layer is a *fixed topology graph*\n* Neighborhood functions live here, not in input space\n\n### 3.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.1 – The Map Grid as an Elastic Net**.\n\n---\n\n# 🟪 STAGE 4 — SOM Grid in Input Space (the classical SOM visualization)\n\n### This is *the missing view you will add next*.\n\n### 4.1 Concept\n\nMap the **output grid** into **input space**:\n\n* For each unit, take its 2D grid coordinate (i,j)\n* Draw a small line or arrow from (i,j) to its weight vector projected into input space\n\nThis is the canonical SOM illustration.\n\n### 4.2 GT View\n\n`mappedGridInInputSpace`\nTwo variants:\n\n#### Variant A — Line connections\n\n* Draw lines connecting neighboring SOM units\n* Each endpoint is positioned at its weight vector projection in input space\n\nResult:\nLearner sees a *“pseudo-elastic net”* deforming to fit data manifold.\n\n#### Variant B — “Spider” layout\n\n* Each node is shown as dot at its weight position\n* Edges drawn between neighbors\n\n### 4.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand the SOM as:\n\n* A continuous mapping\n* A topology-preserving projection\n* A manifold “approximator”\n\n### 4.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.4.1 (input-space ordering)**\nSect. **3.4.2 (output-space ordering)**\nThis view *unifies* these two.\n\n---\n\n# 🟫 STAGE 5 — U-Matrix (Unified Distance Matrix)\n\n### 5.1 Concept\n\nDisplay local distances between neighboring codebook vectors.\n\n### 5.2 GT view\n\n`uMatrix`\n\n* Color-coded\n* Shows cluster structure\n\n### 5.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* Clusters as “hills and valleys”\n* Meaning of magnification factor\n* Why SOM is used for visualization\n\n### 5.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.15 – Using Gray Levels to Indicate Clusters**.\n\n---\n\n# 🟨 STAGE 6 — “Data → Best Matching Unit Map”\n\n### 6.1 Concept\n\nGiven input samples:\nShow how they map to the grid (index of winning neuron).\n\n### 6.2 GT view\n\n`bmuAssignmentPlot`\nDots over grid units, cluster-like patterns.\n\n### 6.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* How the SOM partitions input space\n* Relationship between data density and map density\n\n### 6.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.16 – Interpretation of the SOM Mapping**.\n\n---\n\n# 🟫 STAGE 7 — “Neighborhood Function Dynamics”\n\n### 7.1 Concept\n\nShow how the neighborhood radius shrinks over epochs.\n\n### 7.2 GT view\n\n`radiusTimeline`\n\n* A simple line chart\n\n### 7.3 Learning objective\n\nUnderstand:\n\n* Why global ordering happens early\n* Why fine‐tuning happens late\n\n### 7.4 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.9 – Effect of the neighborhood function**\nSect. **3.8 – Learning rate factor**.\n\n---\n\n# 🟩 STAGE 8 — Batch SOM vs Incremental SOM\n\n### 8.1 Concept\n\nMost students don’t know the difference.\n\n### 8.2 GT views\n\n`batchVsIncrementalComparison`\nOverlay of maps produced by both variants.\n\n### 8.3 Kohonen (2001)\n\nSect. **3.6 – The Batch Map**.\n\n---\n\n# 🟦 STAGE 9 — FolkMemory Interpretation (optional but powerful)\n\n### 9.1 Concept\n\nRewrite SOM learning as:\n\n* distributed objects\n* trail-like radiating influence\n* promotion (winning neuron)\n* diffusion (neighborhood update)\n\nThis beautifully aligns with Ward Cunningham’s *Folk Memory* model.\n\n### 9.2 GT view\n\n`folkMemoryExplanation`\nA narrative view connecting SOM to distributed object propagation.\n\n---\n\n# Summary Table\n\n| Stage | View                                       | Concept                          | Kohonen        |\n| ----- | ------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------- | -------------- |\n| 0     | Weights                                    | raw codebook vectors             | 3.1–3.2        |\n| 1     | weightsAsPoints2D                          | points in input space            | 3.4.1          |\n| 2     | **Mapped Points in Input Space** (rename!) | scaled 2D projection             | 3.4.1          |\n| 3     | gridCoordinates2D                          | the naked map grid               | 3.1            |\n| 4     | mappedGridInInputSpace                     | SOM grid warped into input space | 3.4.1 + 3.4.2  |\n| 5     | uMatrix                                    | cluster visualization            | 3.15           |\n| 6     | bmuAssignmentPlot                          | mapping data onto map            | 3.16           |\n| 7     | radiusTimeline                             | dynamics of neighborhood         | 3.8–3.9        |\n| 8     | batchVsIncrementalComparison               | two training schemes             | 3.6            |\n| 9     | folkMemoryExplanation                      | conceptual metaphor              | FolkMemory.pdf |\n\n---\n\n# Next step:\n\nIf you want, I can generate:\n\n### ✔ A GT-ready **Lepiter curriculum skeleton**\n\n(lessons, pages, anchors, example code, navigation structure)\n\n### ✔ Full code for the next view:\n\n**`mappedGridInInputSpace`**\n\n### ✔ A GT Example suite (green tests)\n\nfor all stages 1–4\n\nJust tell me *which part to produce first*.\n"
			}

The SOM *grid* in input space**\n\n(“mapping the neuron lattice into data space”)\n\n* Each neuron has an index `(i,j)` in the SOM grid.\n* You take each neuron’s weight vector `w(i,j)` in input space.\n* You plot **the weight vector position in input space**, but keep the *neuron lattice* connectivity.\n* This yields a **deformed grid**, still topologically a grid, but warped by the data manifold.\n\nThis is the famous “elastic net” picture.\n\nKohonen 1995, Chapter 3 (“The Basic SOM”), figures 3.3, 3.4.\nAlso in 2001 3rd edition, Chapter 3.\n\n**Expectation:**\n→ A warped but coherent grid.\n→ Topology preserved.\n→ No butterfly.\n\nThis works **only** if your plot preserves **neighbourhoods**.\n\n---\n\n## **2. The raw weight vectors scattered in input space**\n\n(each neuron shown only as a point)\n\nThis is *not* the grid.\nThis is not the map structure.\nThis is just the *set* of weight vectors as points in ℝ².\n\nThis produces:\n\n* Clusters\n* Folds\n* Spirals\n* Butterfly shapes\n* Anything, depending on training parameters and data distribution\n\nKohonen explicitly says:\n\n> “When the neurons are plotted as individual points in input space **without lattice links** the topological structure is not visually evident”\n> *(paraphrased from Kohonen, 1995/2001, Ch. 3)*\n\n**Expectation:**\n→ A cloud of points\n→ No visible grid structure\n→ Possibly self-crossings\n→ Possibly symmetric patterns\n→ “Butterfly” shapes are common in simple 2D input distributions\n\nExactly what you see.\n\n---\n\n# 📌 **Your current '2D Input Space' is #2**\n\nYou’re plotting:\n\n```smalltalk\nweightsAsPoints2DScaledBy: factor\n```\n\nwhich is just the weight vectors in input space (2D), no topology, no connectivity.\n\n**So seeing a butterfly is NORMAL.**\nIt is mathematically valid.\nIt is exactly what the textbook predicts for raw weight scatter.\n\n---\n\n# ⭐ What you actually want (according to the textbook):\n\n## **visualize the SOM lattice mapped into input space**\n\nThat requires **plotting the neuron grid connections**, not just dots.\n\nKohonen figures always show:\n\n* dots = neurons (their weight vectors)\n* lines = connections to right and bottom neighbours in the lattice\n\nThis produces the canonical SOM picture:\n\n```\n(0,0)----(0,1)----(0,2)\n  |        |        |\n(1,0)----(1,1)----(1,2)\n  |        |        |\n(2,0)----(2,1)----(2,2)\n```\n\n…but warped by the data manifold.\n\nThis is what preserves topology.\n\n---\n\n# 🎯 **Next Step: Build the textbook SOM visualization**\n\nYou can implement this cleanly:\n\n### Step A — For each pair of neighbours,\n\ndraw a line between their 2D points:\n\n```smalltalk\nfor each neuron (i,j):\n    draw line from weights[i,j] to weights[i+1,j]   \"down\"\n    draw line from weights[i,j] to weights[i,j+1]   \"right\"\n```\n\nIn GT:\n\n```smalltalk\nroot addChild:\n    (BlLineElement new\n        start: p1;\n        end: p2;\n        border: (Color gray).\n```\n\n### Step B — Plot the nodes exactly like you already do.\n\nThis will yield:\n\n* A fully connected mesh\n* A warped 2D sheet\n* Topology preserved\n* Exactly what Kohonen calls *“mapping the codebook vectors into input space”*\n\nAnd **this** will look like the textbook, not like a butterfly.\n\n---\n\n# 🧭 Summary\n\nYour current view shows pure weight scatter → **no topology → butterfly**\nExpected textbook view shows neuron lattice mapped into input space → **grid-like mesh**\n\nSo the appearance you see is **not a bug, just a different visualization**.\n\nIf you want, I can now:\n\n### ✔︎ Add topology lines (neighbour connections)\n\n### ✔︎ Produce a full SOM elastic-net visualization\n\n### ✔︎ Add zoom and panning\n\n### ✔︎ Add coloring by quantization error or distance\n\nJust tell me “build the SOM lattice view” and I’ll generate the exact GT code.\n"

How graph-algorithms relates to the *som* project nodes\n\nThink in terms of “conversation nodes” you’ve already been circling around:\n\n### a) SOM grids and graph generators\n\nIn *som* you already have:\n\n* `KohonenSom` + `weightsAsPoints2D`\n* Discussions about grids (rectangular / hexagonal neighbourhoods)\n* A wish for multiple **visualizations of the input space**\n\nIn **graph-algorithms** you have:\n\n* `AIGrid2DGenerator`, `AIHexagonalLatticeGenerator`, `AIKleinbergGraphGenerator`, etc., plus examples via `AIGrid2DGenerator class >> example1` etc. \n\nThese generator classes **are exactly** SOM-style neighbourhood graphs:\n\n* Each SOM unit = a **node**\n* Adjacency (4- or 8-neighbourhood, hex, small-world) = **edges**\n* You can treat these lattice graphs as:\n\n  * The **output space** structure of a SOM\n  * A playground for experimenting with *topology* before adding learning rules\n\nSo: one clear “node” in your som conversation graph is *“SOM neighbourhood lattice”* → directly backed by **AI-Algorithms-Graph-Generators**.\n\n---\n\n### b) Distances and neighbourhoods in input space\n\nIn SOM:\n\n* You repeatedly talk about **input space** structure, distances, nearest neighbours, and visualizing `weightsAsPoints2D`.\n* Conceptually, you are building something like a **k-NN graph** over input samples or weight vectors.\n\nIn graph-algorithms:\n\n* `AIBFS`, `AIDijkstra`, `AIBellmanFord`, `AIShortestPathInDAG`, `AILongestPathInDAG`, etc.\n* These give you *path-based* notions of proximity / connectivity:\n\nMapping to SOM:\n\n* **k-nearest-neighbour graph of inputs** → use weighted edges (distance or similarity) and run:\n\n  * `AIDijkstra` for shortest “semantic” paths through the data manifold.\n  * `AIBFS` for unweighted reachability / hop-radius neighbourhoods.\n* On the **SOM lattice graph**, “neighbourhood radius” is literally “all nodes with shortest-path distance ≤ r from the BMU” → directly yielded by BFS or Dijkstra.\n\nSo another “conversation node” is *“neighbourhood function around BMUs”* → formally a **shortest-path / BFS layer** from graph-algorithms.\n\n---\n\n### c) Curriculum & Basic SOM chapter\n\nIn the **gt-curriculum** work you asked:\n\n> “create all the necessary lessons and concepts needed for the Newcomer profile to understand ‘The Basic SOM’ chapter and experiment with different visualizations of the input space.”\n\nThe *PharoGraphs* booklet’s structure gives you a **natural prerequisite track**:\n\n1. **Basic definitions & graph representation** (Ch. 2–3) →\n   Learner becomes fluent with `AIGraphAlgorithm`, `nodes:`, `edges:from:to:`, `edges:from:to:weight:`.\n2. **Traversal & ordering**:\n\n   * BFS (shortest path on unweighted graphs)\n   * Topological sort (`AITopologicalSorting`)\n3. **Weighted distances**:\n\n   * `AIDijkstra`, `AIBellmanFord` → distance on weighted graphs.\n4. **Structure discovery**:\n\n   * `AITarjan` (SCC), `AIKruskal` / `AIPrim` (MST), `AIHits` (link analysis), matchings.\n\nThen Basic SOM chapter plugs in as:\n\n* **Output-space topology**: reuse the lattice / generator examples.\n* **Input-space structure**: reuse shortest-path examples, but with weight vectors instead of toy labels.\n* **Visual experiments**: GT `gtExamples` that *first* show raw graph structures, *then* show SOM views (`weightsAsPoints2D`) on top of similar layouts.\n\nSo in your “conversation topic map”, **graph-algorithms** is the *foundational graph-theory spine* that feeds directly into:\n\n* *“SOM lattice topology”*\n* *“Neighbourhood / radius / distance”*\n* *“Input-space graph visualizations”*\n* *“GT-curriculum: prerequisites for Basic SOM”*\n\n---\n\n## 2. pharo-code-emitter: gtExamples for *PharoGraphs*\n\nBelow is a **single do-it** that:\n\n1. Defines a class `AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples` in package\n   `AI-Algorithms-Graph-GT-Examples`.\n2. Adds a set of **class-side `<gtExample>` methods** corresponding roughly to the chapters of the *PharoGraphs* booklet:\n\n* Basic graph description\n* Topological sorting\n* BFS shortest path\n* Dijkstra shortest path\n* MST (Kruskal)\n* Strongly Connected Components (Tarjan)\n* HITS link analysis\n* Matching (greedy)\n* A SOM-flavoured grid example that bridges to your som project via `AIGrid2DGenerator`.\n\nYou can paste this into a Playground and *do it*.\n\n---\n\n### pharo-code-emitter:\n\n```smalltalk\n\"Create the examples class\"\n\nObject subclass: #AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples\n    instanceVariableNames: ''\n    classVariableNames: ''\n    package: 'AI-Algorithms-Graph-GT-Examples'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"A) Basic graph – chapter 3 style (adjacency list, unweighted)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nbasicUnweightedGraph\n    <gtExample>\n    | algo |\n    \"Example for PharoGraphs, chapter 3: Graph Representation.\n    A small directed graph A → B, A → C, B → C.\"\n    algo := AIGraphAlgorithm new.\n    algo\n        nodes: #( $A $B $C );\n        edges: #(\n            #( $A $B )\n            #( $A $C )\n            #( $B $C )\n        ) from: #first to: #second.\n    ^ algo'\n    classified: 'examples - basic'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"B) Basic weighted graph – chapter 3 (edges:from:to:weight:)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nbasicWeightedGraph\n    <gtExample>\n    | algo |\n    \"Example for PharoGraphs, section on weighted graphs.\"\n    algo := AIGraphAlgorithm new.\n    algo\n        nodes: #( $A $B $C );\n        edges: #(\n            #( $A $B 2 )\n            #( $A $C 4 )\n            #( $B $C 7 )\n        )\n        from: #first\n        to: #second\n        weight: #third.\n    ^ algo'\n    classified: 'examples - basic'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"C) Topological sorting – software modules (chapter 4)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\ntopologicalSortModules\n    <gtExample>\n    | sorter nodes edges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 4: A DAG representing module dependencies.\n     This is essentially the book''s software-modules example.\"\n    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F $G ).\n    edges := #(\n        #( $A $B )\n        #( $A $C )\n        #( $B $E )\n        #( $C $E )\n        #( $C $D )\n        #( $D $E )\n        #( $D $F )\n        #( $E $G )\n        #( $F $G )\n    ).\n    sorter := AITopologicalSorting new.\n    sorter\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.\n    ^ sorter run  \"returns an OrderedCollection of models\"'\n    classified: 'examples - topo sort'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"D) BFS shortest path on unweighted graph (chapter 5 – BFS)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nbfsShortestPathExample\n    <gtExample>\n    | bfs nodes edges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 5: shortest path on unweighted graph via BFS.\n     Simple toy graph from the booklet pattern.\"\n    nodes := $A to: $I.\n    edges := #(\n        #( $A $B ) #( $B $C ) #( $C $D ) #( $D $E ) #( $E $A )\n        #( $B $E ) #( $E $B ) #( $E $F ) #( $F $G ) #( $G $H )\n        #( $H $F ) #( $G $I ) #( $I $G )\n    ).\n    bfs := AIBFS new.\n    bfs\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.\n    ^ bfs runFrom: $A to: $G  \"returns the path as a LinkedList of chars\"'\n    classified: 'examples - shortest path'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"E) Dijkstra shortest path on weighted graph (chapter 5 – Dijkstra)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\ndijkstraShortestPathExample\n    <gtExample>\n    | dijkstra nodes edges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 5: Dijkstra on a small weighted graph.\"\n    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F $G ).\n    edges := #(\n        #( $A $B 1 )\n        #( $A $C 4 )\n        #( $B $C 2 )\n        #( $B $D 5 )\n        #( $C $E 1 )\n        #( $D $F 2 )\n        #( $E $D 1 )\n        #( $E $G 3 )\n        #( $F $G 1 )\n    ).\n    dijkstra := AIDijkstra new.\n    dijkstra\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges\n            from: #first\n            to: #second\n            weight: #third.\n    ^ dijkstra runFrom: $A to: $G   \"shortest A→G path\"'\n    classified: 'examples - shortest path'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"F) Minimum Spanning Tree via Kruskal (chapter 6)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nkruskalMstExample\n    <gtExample>\n    | algo nodes edges treeEdges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 6: Kruskal''s algorithm (MST).\"\n    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E ).\n    edges := #(\n        #( $A $B 3 )\n        #( $A $C 1 )\n        #( $B $C 1 )\n        #( $B $D 4 )\n        #( $C $D 2 )\n        #( $C $E 5 )\n        #( $D $E 1 )\n    ).\n    algo := AIKruskal new.\n    algo\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges\n            from: #first\n            to: #second\n            weight: #third.\n    treeEdges := algo run.   \"collection of AIGraphWeightedEdge\"\n    ^ treeEdges collect: [ :e |\n        { e from model. e to model. e weight } ]'\n    classified: 'examples - mst'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"G) Strongly Connected Components (Tarjan, chapter 7)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\ntarjanSccExample\n    <gtExample>\n    | algo nodes edges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 7: Tarjan''s strongly connected components.\"\n    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F ).\n    edges := #(\n        #( $A $B )\n        #( $B $C )\n        #( $C $A )   \"A-B-C forms an SCC\"\n        #( $B $D )\n        #( $D $E )\n        #( $E $D )   \"D-E forms an SCC\"\n        #( $E $F )\n    ).\n    algo := AITarjan new.\n    algo\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.\n    ^ algo stronglyConnectedComponents\n        \"returns #( #( $A $B $C ) #( $D $E ) #( $F ) ) (order may vary)\"'\n    classified: 'examples - scc'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"H) HITS link analysis on a toy web graph (chapter 8)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nhitsToyWebGraph\n    <gtExample>\n    | hits nodes edges |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 8: HITS (hubs & authorities).\"\n    nodes := #( #a #b #c #d ).  \"pages\"\n    edges := #(\n        #( #a #b )\n        #( #a #c )\n        #( #b #c )\n        #( #c #d )\n    ).\n    hits := AIHits new.\n    hits\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.\n    hits run.\n    ^ hits nodes collect: [ :node |\n        { node model. node hub. node auth } ]'\n    classified: 'examples - hits'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"I) Greedy matching on a small bipartite graph (chapter 9)\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\ngreedyMatchingExample\n    <gtExample>\n    | algo nodes edges matching |\n    \"PharoGraphs, chapter 9: greedy matching.\n     U = {a1,a2}, V = {b1,b2,b3}.\"\n    nodes := #( #a1 #a2 #b1 #b2 #b3 ).\n    edges := #(\n        #( #a1 #b1 )\n        #( #a1 #b2 )\n        #( #a2 #b2 )\n        #( #a2 #b3 )\n    ).\n    algo := AIGreedyMatching new.\n    algo\n        nodes: nodes;\n        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.\n    matching := algo run.  \"collection of AIGraphEdge\"\n    ^ matching collect: [ :e |\n        { e from model. e to model } ]'\n    classified: 'examples - matching'.\n```\n\n```smalltalk\n\"J) SOM-flavoured grid graph – bridge into the som project\"\n\nAIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class\n    compile: '\nsomLikeGridGraph\n    <gtExample>\n    | g |\n    \"Bridge to the som project: a 2D grid graph that can be read as\n     a Kohonen map lattice (each node = a unit, edges = neighbours).\n     Uses AIGrid2DGenerator''s existing example API.\"\n    g := AIGrid2DGenerator new\n        width: 10;\n        height: 10;\n        neighborhood: #moore;\n        yourself.\n    g run.\n    \"Return nodes + edges as a tuple-like array for exploration or\n     for feeding a KohonenSom or GT view later.\"\n    ^ { g nodes. g edges }'\n    classified: 'examples - som bridge'.\n```\n\n---\n\n### How to use these in GT\n\n* After evaluating the do-its:\n\n  * Open the **Examples** browser.\n  * Filter by class: `AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples`.\n* Each method is a `<gtExample>`:\n\n  * `basicUnweightedGraph` / `basicWeightedGraph` → directly mirror Ch. 3.\n  * `topologicalSortModules` → Ch. 4.\n  * `bfsShortestPathExample` / `dijkstraShortestPathExample` → Ch. 5.\n  * `kruskalMstExample` → Ch. 6.\n  * `tarjanSccExample` → Ch. 7.\n  * `hitsToyWebGraph` → Ch. 8.\n  * `greedyMatchingExample` → Ch. 9.\n  * `somLikeGridGraph` → **feeds directly into your SOM work** (same style of grid as a SOM lattice).\n\nIf you’d like, next step I can help you:\n\n* Wrap `somLikeGridGraph` into a **KohonenSom**-aware example (`KohonenSom class >> gtExampleGridFromAIGraphAlgorithms`) and\n* Hook these examples into your **gt-curriculum** Lepiter pages as “Graph Algorithms → Basic SOM” prerequisites.\n"
			}
		]

## File: src/AI-Algorithms-Graph-Examples/AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples.class.st
`````
Class {
	#name : #AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples,
	#superclass : #Object,
	#category : #'AI-Algorithms-Graph-Examples-GT-Examples'
}

{ #category : #'examples - basic' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> basicUnweightedGraph [
    <gtExample>
    | algo |
    "Example for PharoGraphs, chapter 3: Graph Representation.
    A small directed graph A → B, A → C, B → C."
    algo := AIGraphAlgorithm new.
    algo
        nodes: #( $A $B $C );
        edges: #(
            #( $A $B )
            #( $A $C )
            #( $B $C )
        ) from: #first to: #second.
    ^ algo
]

{ #category : #'examples - basic' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> basicWeightedGraph [
    <gtExample>
    | algo |
    "Example for PharoGraphs, section on weighted graphs."
    algo := AIGraphAlgorithm new.
    algo
        nodes: #( $A $B $C );
        edges: #(
            #( $A $B 2 )
            #( $A $C 4 )
            #( $B $C 7 )
        )
        from: #first
        to: #second
        weight: #third.
    ^ algo
]

{ #category : #'examples - shortest path' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> bfsShortestPathExample [
    <gtExample>
    | bfs nodes edges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 5: shortest path on unweighted graph via BFS.
     Simple toy graph from the booklet pattern."
    nodes := $A to: $I.
    edges := #(
        #( $A $B ) #( $B $C ) #( $C $D ) #( $D $E ) #( $E $A )
        #( $B $E ) #( $E $B ) #( $E $F ) #( $F $G ) #( $G $H )
        #( $H $F ) #( $G $I ) #( $I $G )
    ).
    bfs := AIBFS new.
    bfs
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.
    ^ bfs runFrom: $A to: $G  "returns the path as a LinkedList of chars"
]

{ #category : #'examples - shortest path' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> dijkstraShortestPathExample [
    <gtExample>
    | dijkstra nodes edges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 5: Dijkstra on a small weighted graph."
    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F $G ).
    edges := #(
        #( $A $B 1 )
        #( $A $C 4 )
        #( $B $C 2 )
        #( $B $D 5 )
        #( $C $E 1 )
        #( $D $F 2 )
        #( $E $D 1 )
        #( $E $G 3 )
        #( $F $G 1 )
    ).
    dijkstra := AIDijkstra new.
    dijkstra
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges
            from: #first
            to: #second
            weight: #third.
    ^ dijkstra runFrom: $A to: $G   "shortest A→G path"
]

{ #category : #'examples - matching' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> greedyMatchingExample [
    <gtExample>
    | algo nodes edges matching |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 9: greedy matching.
     U = {a1,a2}, V = {b1,b2,b3}."
    nodes := #( #a1 #a2 #b1 #b2 #b3 ).
    edges := #(
        #( #a1 #b1 )
        #( #a1 #b2 )
        #( #a2 #b2 )
        #( #a2 #b3 )
    ).
    algo := AIGreedyMatching new.
    algo
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.
    matching := algo run.  "collection of AIGraphEdge"
    ^ matching collect: [ :e |
        { e from model. e to model } ]
]

{ #category : #'examples - hits' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> hitsToyWebGraph [
    <gtExample>
    | hits nodes edges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 8: HITS (hubs & authorities)."
    nodes := #( #a #b #c #d ).  "pages"
    edges := #(
        #( #a #b )
        #( #a #c )
        #( #b #c )
        #( #c #d )
    ).
    hits := AIHits new.
    hits
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.
    hits run.
    ^ hits nodes collect: [ :node |
        { node model. node hub. node auth } ]
]

{ #category : #'examples - mst' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> kruskalMstExample [
    <gtExample>
    | algo nodes edges treeEdges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 6: Kruskal's algorithm (MST)."
    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E ).
    edges := #(
        #( $A $B 3 )
        #( $A $C 1 )
        #( $B $C 1 )
        #( $B $D 4 )
        #( $C $D 2 )
        #( $C $E 5 )
        #( $D $E 1 )
    ).
    algo := AIKruskal new.
    algo
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges
            from: #first
            to: #second
            weight: #third.
    treeEdges := algo run.   "collection of AIGraphWeightedEdge"
    ^ treeEdges collect: [ :e |
        { e from model. e to model. e weight } ]
]

{ #category : #'examples - som bridge' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> somLikeGridGraph [
    <gtExample>
    | g |
    "Bridge to the som project: a 2D grid graph that can be read as
     a Kohonen map lattice (each node = a unit, edges = neighbours).
     Uses AIGrid2DGenerator's existing example API."
    g := AIGrid2DGenerator new
        width: 10;
        height: 10;
        neighborhood: #moore;
        yourself.
    g run.
    "Return nodes + edges as a tuple-like array for exploration or
     for feeding a KohonenSom or GT view later."
    ^ { g nodes. g edges }
]

{ #category : #'examples - scc' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> tarjanSccExample [
    <gtExample>
    | algo nodes edges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 7: Tarjan's strongly connected components."
    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F ).
    edges := #(
        #( $A $B )
        #( $B $C )
        #( $C $A )   "A-B-C forms an SCC"
        #( $B $D )
        #( $D $E )
        #( $E $D )   "D-E forms an SCC"
        #( $E $F )
    ).
    algo := AITarjan new.
    algo
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.
    ^ algo stronglyConnectedComponents
        "returns #( #( $A $B $C ) #( $D $E ) #( $F ) ) (order may vary)"
]

{ #category : #'examples - topo sort' }
AIGraphAlgorithmsGtExamples class >> topologicalSortModules [
    <gtExample>
    | sorter nodes edges |
    "PharoGraphs, chapter 4: A DAG representing module dependencies.
     This is essentially the book's software-modules example."
    nodes := #( $A $B $C $D $E $F $G ).
    edges := #(
        #( $A $B )
        #( $A $C )
        #( $B $E )
        #( $C $E )
        #( $C $D )
        #( $D $E )
        #( $D $F )
        #( $E $G )
        #( $F $G )
    ).
    sorter := AITopologicalSorting new.
    sorter
        nodes: nodes;
        edges: edges from: #first to: #second.
    ^ sorter run  "returns an OrderedCollection of models"
]
`````

## File: src/Som-Tests/KohonenSomTest.class.st
`````
Class {
	#name : #KohonenSomTest,
	#superclass : #TestCase,
	#category : #'Som-Tests'
}

{ #category : #tests }
KohonenSomTest >> testBestMatchingUnitReasonable [
    | som input winnerVector winnerDistance |
    som := KohonenSom new
        initializeWithInputDimension: 2
        width: 3
        height: 3
        iterations: 1.
    
    input := { 0.5. 0.5 } asArray.
    winnerVector := som weights at: (som bestMatchingUnitIndexFor: input).
    winnerDistance := som
        distanceSquaredBetween: winnerVector
        and: input.
    
    som weights do: [ :w |
        self assert: (som distanceSquaredBetween: w and: input) >= winnerDistance ]
]

{ #category : #tests }
KohonenSomTest >> testInitializationShapes [
    | som |
    som := KohonenSom new
        initializeWithInputDimension: 3
        width: 5
        height: 4
        iterations: 10.
    
    self assert: som weights size equals: 5 * 4.
    som weights do: [ :w |
        self assert: w size equals: 3 ]
]

{ #category : #tests }
KohonenSomTest >> testWeightsChangeAfterTraining [
    | som data before after |
    som := KohonenSom new
        initializeWithInputDimension: 2
        width: 3
        height: 3
        iterations: 20.
    
    data := #( {0.0. 0.0} {1.0. 1.0} ) collect: #asArray.
    before := som weights collect: [ :w | w collect: [ :v | v ] ].
    
    som trainOn: data.
    after := som weights.
    
    self deny: (before = after)
]
`````

Define how items are positioned\"\n            m layout custom\n                node: [ :node :p | \n                    \"p is the model (a Point like 10@10, 50@20, ...)\"\n                    node position: p ] ]\n```\n\nNow try again with:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10. 50@20. 30@80 } inspect\n```\n\nand pick **“2D Input Space”**.\n\nYou should see three small blue dots at those coordinates. Primer on Kohonen SOM Data for Visualization**\n\n### **Lesson 6 – What is `weightsAsPoints2D`?**\n\nYour question: *“Explain what we see in weightsAsPoints2D.”*\n\nAnswer (to be used in the lesson):\n\n**`weightsAsPoints2D` is the 2-dimensional embedding of each neuron’s weight vector.**\nTypically:\n\n* Each neuron i has weight vector `w_i = (w1, w2, …, wn)`.\n* For visualization we choose:\n\n  * either the first two components\n  * or a projection (PCA)\n  * or a grid coordinate + color coding\n\n**weightsAsPoints2D = Collection of {x,y} pairs for each neuron.**\n\nThis is the *input* for scatter plots, U-Matrix visualizations, component planes, etc.\n\n### **Lesson 7 – Where this appears in Kohonen (1995)**\n\nUse **Kohonen 2001** / **1995** Ch. 3 (Basic SOM):\n\n* §3.1–3.4 explain topology preservation\n* §3.14 shows examples of 2D maps of high-dimensional weight vectors.\n  This is exactly where the idea of projecting weights into 2D for visualization is introduced.\n\n---\n\n# **4. GT View Integration (KohonenSom Path)**\n\nNow we move to creating GT views analogous to the Plotter examples.\n\n### **Lesson 8 – GT View Anatomy**\n\nIntroduce:\n\n```smalltalk\n<gtView>\n^ aView forward\n    title: 'weightsAsPoints2D';\n    object: [ self weightsAsPoints2D asGtJson ];\n    view: #gtJsonObjectFor:context:\n```\n\nExplain:\n\n* `aView forward` = same pattern used in Plotter examples\n* mapping model → view → widget\n* For KohonenSom we will switch view to Plotter scatter\n\n### **Lesson 9 – KohonenSom>>#gtWeightsOn: (1D plot)**\n\nDesign a view that plots only weight magnitudes or single component over neurons.\n\nConcept:\n\n```smalltalk\n<gtView>\n^ aView forward\n   title: 'SOM weight distributions';\n   object: [ self weights ]; \n   view: #gtPlotterOfWeightsOn:\n```\n\nThen implement `gtPlotterOfWeightsOn:` to create a bar chart or line chart.\n\n### **Lesson 10 – KohonenSom>>#gtWeights2DOn: (2D scatter)**\n\nThis is the Plotter scatter lesson applied to SOM:\n\n```smalltalk\ngtWeights2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    | pts data scatter |\n    pts := self weightsAsPoints2D.\n    data := GtPlotterDataGroup new values: pts.\n    scatter := GtPlotterScatterPlot new\n        x: [:p | p first];\n        y: [:p | p second];\n        with: data.\n    ^ aView explicit stencil: scatter\n```\n\nHere the Newcomer should clearly see:\n\n* *Plotter data group* ← points\n* *Scatter plot mapping* ← x: y:\n* *Visualization* ← exactly same as Plotter examples\n\n---\n"

				"string" : "## 1. A working version of `gtScatter2DOn:`\n\nAssuming:\n\n* `self` is a `Collection` of **Points** (`10@20`, `30@40`, …)\n* You want a small dot for each point in input space\n\nThen:\n\n```smalltalk\nCollection>>gtScatter2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView mondrian\n        title: '2D Input Space';\n        painting: [ :m |\n            m nodes\n                shape: [ :p | \n                    BlElement new\n                        size: 4 @ 4;\n                        geometry: BlEllipseGeometry new;\n                        background: Color blue;\n                        yourself ];\n                translate: [ :p | p ];  \"Position = the Point itself\"\n                with: self ]\n```\n\nKey differences vs your version:\n\n1. **`yourself` at the end of the shape block**\n\n   * `geometry:` usually returns the geometry, **not** the element, so without `yourself` the shape block returns a `BlEllipseGeometry` instead of a `BlElement`.\n   * Mondrian expects the shape block to return a `BlElement`.\n   * `yourself` ensures the last returned object is the configured `BlElement`.\n\n2. **`translate:` (position)**\n\n   * Without any layout or translation, everything is at `(0@0)` and may be outside the visible region or all on top of each other.\n   * `translate: [:p | p]` uses the point as its own position → classic 2D scatter.\n\n3. Using `with: self` is fine if `self` is the collection you want to plot.\n\nTry this with something like:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10. 50@20. 30@80 } inspect\n```\n\nThen choose the **“2D Input Space”** view in the inspector.\n\n---\n\n## 2. How to debug Mondrian views when nothing shows\n\nHere’s a practical checklist:\n\n### (a) Check the view is actually invoked\n\nTemporarily add:\n\n```smalltalk\npainting: [ :m |\n    Transcript show: 'gtScatter2DOn painting'; cr.\n    ...\n]\n```\n\nIf you don’t see this in the Transcript, either:\n\n* the method isn’t being called (wrong class / selector), or\n* you’re looking at a different view in the inspector.\n\n### (b) Check your collection isn’t empty\n\nInside `painting:`:\n\n```smalltalk\nself isEmpty ifTrue: [\n    Transcript show: 'Collection is empty'; cr.\n].\n```\n\n### (c) Inspect what the shape block returns\n\nAdd a tiny self-check:\n\n```smalltalk\nm nodes\n    shape: [ :p | \n        | e |\n        e := BlElement new\n                size: 4 @ 4;\n                geometry: BlEllipseGeometry new;\n                background: Color blue;\n                yourself.\n        (e isKindOf: BlElement)\n            ifFalse: [ self error: 'Shape does not return a BlElement' ].\n        e ];\n    translate: [ :p | p ];\n    with: self\n```\n\nIf that error fires, you know the shape contract is wrong.\n\n### (d) Verify positions\n\nIf your elements later are **not** Points but some objects, decide how to get coordinates:\n\n```smalltalk\ntranslate: [ :obj | obj position ]  \"if obj has #position\"\n```\n\nOr:\n\n```smalltalk\ntranslate: [ :obj | obj x @ obj y ]\n```\n\nIf you don’t set either `translate:` (or a layout), nodes may all pile up at the origin.\n\n### (e) Try with a tiny, known collection\n\nBefore you use your full SOM input set, try:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10. 20@30. 40@10 } inspect\n```\n\nIf that works, the Mondrian code is fine and any remaining problem is in your SOM data.\n\n---\n\nIf you paste the corrected `Collection>>gtScatter2DOn:` above, you should see a small blue-dot scatter plot. From there we can refine it into a dedicated `KohonenSom>>gtWeights2DOn:` that uses `weightsAsPoints2D`.\n"
			}
		]

linear scale, data group).\n\n### `SequenceableCollection>>asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart`\n\n```smalltalk\nSequenceableCollection>>asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart\n    <gtExample>\n    <return: #GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart>\n    | theData maxX xScale chart |\n\n    \"Assume self is a sequence of Points (x@y).\"\n    self isEmpty ifTrue: [ ^ GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart new ].\n\n    \"Wrap each point in a small dictionary with #index and #x/#y.\"\n    theData := GtPlotterDataGroup new\n        values: (self collectWithIndex: [ :p :index |\n            Dictionary newFrom: {\n                #index -> index.\n                #x     -> p x.\n                #y     -> p y } ]).\n\n    \"Labels: p1, p2, p3, ...\"\n    theData := theData\n        labelled: [ :each | 'p', (each at: #index) asString ].\n\n    \"Colour based on y, purely to use the second coordinate somehow.\"\n    theData := theData\n        background: [ :each |\n            | y |\n            y := each at: #y.\n            y >= 0\n                ifTrue: [ Color\n                            r: 66\n                            g: 188\n                            b: 238\n                            range: 255 ]\n                ifFalse: [ Color\n                            r: 216\n                            g: 55\n                            b: 62\n                            range: 255 ] ].\n\n    \"Scale the bar width from 0 .. max x.\"\n    maxX := theData\n        inject: 0\n        intoValues: [ :currentMax :each |\n            currentMax max: (each at: #x) ].\n\n    xScale := GtPlotterLinearScale new\n        domainFrom: 0\n        to: maxX.\n\n    chart := GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart new.\n    chart\n        barLabelSpacing: 50;\n        barWidthScale: xScale;\n        barWidthData: [ :each | each at: #x ];\n        amountOfTicks: 4;\n        with: theData.\n\n    ^ chart\n```\n\n### How to test it (no GT view involved yet)\n\nIn a playground:\n\n```smalltalk\n{ 10@10 . 50@20 . 30@80 } asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart\n```\n\nEvaluate and inspect the result – you should see a bar chart:\n\n* each bar = one point,\n* bar length = x-coordinate,\n* colour = derived from y.\n\nIf you still see the `Collection had the subclass responsibility to implement #do:` error **here**, that means you really are sending this to something like `Collection new` instead of to a `SequenceableCollection` (e.g. an `Array`). The literal `{ ... }` form is an `Array`, so it should be safe.\n\n---\n"
			},
			{
				"__type" : "textSnippet",
				"children" : {
					"__type" : "snippets",
					"items" : [ ]
				},
				"createEmail" : {
					"__type" : "email",
					"emailString" : "<unknown>"
				},
				"createTime" : {
					"__type" : "time",
					"time" : {
						"__type" : "dateAndTime",
						"dateAndTimeString" : "2025-11-16T23:00:05.987146+01:00"
					}
				},
				"editEmail" : {
					"__type" : "email",
					"emailString" : "<unknown>"
				},
				"editTime" : {
					"__type" : "time",
					"time" : {
						"__type" : "dateAndTime",
						"dateAndTimeString" : "2025-11-16T23:00:17.260664+01:00"
					}
				},
				"uid" : {
					"__type" : "uid",
					"uidString" : "py0hFx8ADgC7ZccbCw+Ujg=="
				},
				"paragraphStyle" : {
					"__type" : "textStyle"
				},
				"string" : "## 3. Wire it back into your `Collection>>gtScatter2DOn:`\n\nNow that the helper lives on `SequenceableCollection`, you can keep your GT view on `Collection` and just call the helper on `self` (which, in the inspector, will actually be an `Array`, `OrderedCollection`, etc.):\n\n```smalltalk\nCollection>>gtScatter2DOn: aView\n    <gtView>\n    ^ aView forward\n        title: '2D Input Space';\n        object: [ \n            self isKindOf: SequenceableCollection\n                ifTrue: [ self asGtPlotterInputSpaceChart ]\n                ifFalse: [ GtPlotterHorizontalBarChart new ] ];\n        view: #gtInspectorViewFor:context:\n```\n\nSo:\n\n1. The heavy lifting is on `SequenceableCollection`.\n2. The `gtView` method on `Collection` just forwards if the receiver is a sequence-type collection, and otherwise returns an empty chart instead of crashing.\n\n---\n"
			},
			{

				"children" : {

## File: src/Som-Examples/KohonenSomExamples.class.st
`````
Class {
	#name : #KohonenSomExamples,
	#superclass : #Object,
	#category : #'Som-Examples'
}

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSomExamples class >> exampleInputSpace2D [
    <gtExample>
    "Generate random 2D input samples and visualize them."
    
    | data |
    data := (1 to: 500) collect: [ :i |
        (Random new next) @ (Random new next) ].

    ^ data
]

{ #category : #examples }
KohonenSomExamples class >> exampleUnitSquare2D [
	"Train a small SOM on random points in the unit square."

	<gtExample>
	| data som numberOfSamples |
	numberOfSamples := 500.
	data := (1 to: numberOfSamples)
			collect: [ :i | 
				{Random new next.
					Random new next} asArray ].

	som := KohonenSom new
			initializeWithInputDimension: 2
			width: 10
			height: 10
			iterations: 2000.

	som trainOn: data.
	^ som
]

{ #category : #examples }
KohonenSomExamples class >> exampleWeightCoordinates2D [
    <gtExample>
    "Return a collection of Points representing weight vectors in 2D."
    
    | som coords |
    som := self exampleUnitSquare2D.
    coords := som weights collect: [ :w |
        (w size >= 2)
            ifTrue: [ (w first) @ (w second) ]
            ifFalse: [ 0 @ 0 ] ].
    ^ coords
]
`````

## File: src/Som-Core/KohonenSom.class.st
`````
Class {
	#name : #KohonenSom,
	#superclass : #Object,
	#instVars : [
		'inputDimension',
		'width',
		'height',
		'weights',
		'maxIterations',
		'iterationCount',
		'initialLearningRate',
		'initialRadius',
		'learningTimeConstant',
		'radiusTimeConstant',
		'zoomFactor'
	],
	#category : #'Som-Core'
}

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> bestMatchingUnitIndexFor: inputVector [
    "Return the index of the weight vector closest to inputVector."
    
    | bestIndex bestDistance |
    bestIndex := nil.
    bestDistance := nil.
    1 to: weights size do: [ :i |
        | d |
        d := self distanceSquaredBetween: (weights at: i) and: inputVector.
        (bestDistance isNil or: [ d < bestDistance ]) ifTrue: [
            bestDistance := d.
            bestIndex := i ] ].
    ^ bestIndex
]

{ #category : #metrics }
KohonenSom >> distanceSquaredBetween: v1 and: v2 [
    "Squared Euclidean distance between two vectors (Arrays of numbers)."
    
    | sum |
    sum := 0.0.
    1 to: inputDimension do: [ :k |
        | d |
        d := (v1 at: k) - (v2 at: k).
        sum := sum + (d * d) ].
    ^ sum
]

{ #category : #geometry }
KohonenSom >> gridDistanceSquaredFrom: p1 to: p2 [
    "Squared Euclidean distance on the neuron grid."
    
    | dx dy |
    dx := p1 x - p2 x.
    dy := p1 y - p2 y.
    ^ (dx * dx) + (dy * dy)
]

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSom >> gtJsonFor: aView [
	<gtView>
	^ aView forward
		title: 'weightsAsPoints2D';
		object: [ self weightsAsPoints2D asGtJson ];
		view: #gtJsonObjectFor:context:
]

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSom >> gtWeightVectorsInInputSpaceOn: aView [
	<gtView>
	^ aView explicit
		title: 'Codebook Scatter';
		stencil: [ :presentation | 
			| root scaledPoints |
			root := BlElement new
					size: 600 @ 600;
					background: Color white;
					yourself.

			scaledPoints := self weightsAsPoints2DScaledBy: self zoomFactor.

			scaledPoints
				do: [ :p "p is a scaled Point in pixel space" | 
					| dot |
					dot := BlElement new
							size: 12 @ 12;
							geometry: BlEllipseGeometry new;
							background: Color blue;
							relocate: p;
							yourself.
					root addChild: dot ].

			root ]
]

{ #category : #'gt-views' }
KohonenSom >> gtWeights2DOn: aView [
	<gtView>
	^ aView mondrian
		title: 'Weights (Input Space, 2D)';
		painting: [ :m "self weightsAsPoints2D should answer a collection of Points" | 
			m nodes
				stencil: [ :p | 
					BlElement new
						geometry: BlEllipseGeometry new;
						size: 4 @ 4;
						background: Color blue ];
				with: self weightsAsPoints2D.	"For a first working version, just use a built-in layout"
			m layout circle radius: 50 ]
]

{ #category : #'gt-views' }
KohonenSom >> gtWeightsOn: aView [
	<gtView>
	^ aView forward
		title: 'Weights';
		object: [ weights ]
]

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSom >> gtZoomOn: aView [
    <gtView>
    ^ aView text
        title: 'Zoom factor';
        priority: 5;
        text: [ self zoomFactor asString ]

]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> height [
    ^ height
]

{ #category : #initialization }
KohonenSom >> initializeRandomWeights [
    "Initialize all weight vectors with random values in [0, 1]."
    
    | numberOfNeurons |
    numberOfNeurons := width * height.
    weights := Array new: numberOfNeurons.
    1 to: numberOfNeurons do: [ :i |
        weights
            at: i
            put: (Array new: inputDimension
                streamContents: [ :stream |
                    1 to: inputDimension do: [ :k |
                        stream nextPut: (Random new next) ] ]) ]
]

{ #category : #initialization }
KohonenSom >> initializeWithInputDimension: anInteger width: aWidth height: aHeight iterations: totalIterations [
    inputDimension := anInteger.
    width := aWidth.
    height := aHeight.
    maxIterations := totalIterations.
    iterationCount := 0.
    initialLearningRate := 0.1.
    initialRadius := (width max: height) / 2.0.
    learningTimeConstant := maxIterations asFloat / 2.0.
    radiusTimeConstant := maxIterations asFloat / (initialRadius ln).
    self initializeRandomWeights.
    ^ self
]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> inputDimension [
    ^ inputDimension
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> learningRateAtTime: t [
    "Exponential decay of the learning rate.
    t is zero-based iteration index."
    
    ^ initialLearningRate * (Float e raisedTo: (t negated / learningTimeConstant))
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> neighborhoodInfluenceAtTime: t winnerIndex: winnerIndex neuronIndex: neuronIndex [
    "Gaussian neighborhood h_ci(t) in the neuron grid."
    
    | sigma2 dist2 |
    sigma2 := (self radiusAtTime: t) squared.
    sigma2 = 0 ifTrue: [ ^ 0 ].
    dist2 := self
        gridDistanceSquaredFrom: (self positionOfIndex: winnerIndex)
        to: (self positionOfIndex: neuronIndex).
    ^ Float e raisedTo: (dist2 negated / (2.0 * sigma2))
]

{ #category : #geometry }
KohonenSom >> positionOfIndex: index [
    "Return the 2D grid coordinates (x @ y) for a 1-based linear index."
    
    | zeroBased x y |
    zeroBased := index - 1.
    x := (zeroBased \\ width).
    y := (zeroBased // width).
    ^ x @ y
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> radiusAtTime: t [
    "Exponential decay of the neighborhood radius."
    
    ^ initialRadius * (Float e raisedTo: (t negated / radiusTimeConstant))
]

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSom >> scaledWeightsAsPoints2DForCanvas: canvasExtent [
	"Return points scaled so that *all* weightsAsPoints2D fit
	 into a rectangle 0@0 corner: canvasExtent, with a small margin."

	| pts minX maxX minY maxY spanX spanY scaleX scaleY margin |

	pts := self weightsAsPoints2D.
	pts isEmpty ifTrue: [ ^ #() ].

	"Find bounding box in input space"
	minX := maxX := pts first x.
	minY := maxY := pts first y.
	pts do: [ :p |
		minX := minX min: p x.
		maxX := maxX max: p x.
		minY := minY min: p y.
		maxY := maxY max: p y ].

	spanX := (maxX - minX) max: 1e-6.
	spanY := (maxY - minY) max: 1e-6.

	margin := 10.  "pixels"

	scaleX := (canvasExtent x - (2 * margin)) / spanX.
	scaleY := (canvasExtent y - (2 * margin)) / spanY.

	^ pts collect: [ :p |
		| nx ny |
		nx := margin + (p x - minX) * scaleX.
		ny := margin + (p y - minY) * scaleY.
		nx @ ny ]

]

{ #category : #'batch-training' }
KohonenSom >> trainBatchOn: aCollection iterations: batchIterations [
    "Skeleton for the Batch Map algorithm (Sec. 3.14).
    For now, this just calls the online trainer; fill with
    the true batch algorithm later."
    
    ^ self trainOn: aCollection
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> trainOn: aCollection [
    "Train the SOM for maxIterations iterations, cycling through aCollection."
    
    1 to: maxIterations do: [ :t |
        | index input |
        index := ((t - 1) \\ aCollection size) + 1.
        input := aCollection at: index.
        self trainOne: input atTime: t - 1 ].
    ^ self
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> trainOne: inputVector atTime: t [
    "Perform one SOM update step for a single input vector."
    
    | eta winner radius |
    eta := self learningRateAtTime: t.
    winner := self bestMatchingUnitIndexFor: inputVector.
    radius := self radiusAtTime: t.  "not used directly but makes intent explicit"
    
    1 to: weights size do: [ :i |
        | h |
        h := self
            neighborhoodInfluenceAtTime: t
            winnerIndex: winner
            neuronIndex: i.
        self
            updateNeuronAt: i
            withInput: inputVector
            learningRate: eta
            neighborhoodInfluence: h ].
    
    iterationCount := iterationCount + 1
]

{ #category : #training }
KohonenSom >> updateNeuronAt: neuronIndex
    withInput: inputVector
    learningRate: eta
    neighborhoodInfluence: h [
    "Apply Kohonen update: m_i <- m_i + eta * h * (x - m_i)."
    
    | w |
    h = 0 ifTrue: [ ^ self ].
    w := weights at: neuronIndex.
    1 to: inputDimension do: [ :k |
        | old delta |
        old := w at: k.
        delta := eta * h * ((inputVector at: k) - old).
        w at: k put: old + delta ]
]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> weights [
    ^ weights
]

{ #category : #converting }
KohonenSom >> weightsAsPoints2D [
    "Return a collection of Points for 2D SOMs (first two components)."
    
    ^ weights collect: [ :w |
        (w size >= 2)
            ifTrue: [ (w first) @ (w second) ]
            ifFalse: [ 0 @ 0 ] ]
]

{ #category : #'as yet unclassified' }
KohonenSom >> weightsAsPoints2DScaledBy: factor [
	"Simple zoom: multiply all coordinates by a scalar.
     Assumes weightsAsPoints2D answers Points (x@y)."

	| pts |
	pts := self weightsAsPoints2D.
	pts isEmpty ifTrue: [ ^ #() ].

	^ pts collect: [ :p | p * factor ]
]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> width [
    ^ width
]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> zoomFactor [
	^ zoomFactor ifNil: [  "default zoom"zoomFactor := 600.0 ]
]

{ #category : #accessing }
KohonenSom >> zoomFactor: aNumber [
	zoomFactor := (aNumber max: 0.01) asFloat	"avoid zero / negative"
]
`````
